# Task: Implement Custom Named Folding Regions with Navigation in VS Code

## Objective
Add support for custom named folding regions in VS Code that can be navigated via a quick-pick menu. Users mark regions with special comments (e.g., `// #region MySection` / `// #endregion`), and this feature extends the existing folding to allow naming and jumping to regions by name.

## Requirements

1. **Create a Named Region Provider** in the folding subsystem:
   - Create or extend a folding range provider in `src/vs/editor/contrib/folding/browser/`
   - Detect `#region <name>` and `#endregion` comment markers
   - Extract the region name from the marker
   - Register named regions in a data structure that maps name -> line range

2. **Add region decoration** in the editor:
   - Display the region name as a decorative label in the gutter or inline
   - Use VS Code's decoration API (`IModelDecorationOptions`)
   - Collapsed regions should show the name in the fold placeholder text

3. **Register a "Go to Region" command**:
   - Add command `editor.action.goToNamedRegion` in `src/vs/editor/contrib/folding/browser/`
   - Wire it to a keybinding (suggest `Ctrl+Shift+R` / `Cmd+Shift+R`)
   - Register the command via `registerEditorAction` or `registerEditorCommand` pattern

4. **Implement quick-pick navigation**:
   - When the command is invoked, show a quick-pick (`IQuickInputService`) listing all named regions in the current file
   - Each item shows the region name and line number
   - Selecting an item navigates the editor cursor to that region and unfolds it

5. **Add a test file** for the named region provider:
   - Test region detection and name extraction
   - Test navigation to a named region

## Key Reference Files
- `src/vs/editor/contrib/folding/browser/folding.ts` — main folding contribution
- `src/vs/editor/contrib/folding/browser/foldingRanges.ts` — FoldingRanges data structure
- `src/vs/editor/contrib/folding/browser/indentRangeProvider.ts` — reference range provider
- `src/vs/editor/contrib/folding/browser/syntaxRangeProvider.ts` — another range provider pattern
- `src/vs/editor/common/model/textModel.ts` — text model API for line access
- `src/vs/editor/contrib/gotoSymbol/browser/goToCommands.ts` — reference for navigation commands
- `src/vs/platform/quickinput/common/quickInput.ts` — QuickInput service interface

## Success Criteria
- Named region detection code exists in folding contrib
- Region name extraction from `#region` markers implemented
- Command registered for navigating to named regions
- Quick-pick integration with region listing
- Decoration or placeholder text shows region names
- Test file exists for the region provider

### Provider Design

The `#region`/`#endregion` pattern is universal (used in C#, Python, TypeScript, etc.).

Pattern:
- `#region` optionally followed by a name: `/^\s*#region\s*(.*)/i` → start
- `#endregion`: `/^\s*#endregion/i` → end

The stack-based approach:
- Scan lines top to bottom
- When we see `#region`, push `{ line, name }` onto a stack
- When we see `#endregion`, pop the stack and create a folding range (startLine → endLine)
- Store the region name in the `types` array of `FoldingRegions`

Looking at `FoldingRegions` constructor:
```ts
constructor(startIndexes: Uint32Array, endIndexes: Uint32Array, types?: Array<string | undefined>)
```

The `types` array is indexed the same as start/endIndexes. So I need to sort ranges by start line (ascending order is required by FoldingRegions).

Actually, looking at `indentRangeProvider.ts` - ranges are inserted with `insertFirst` which builds them in reverse ord

For my implementation:
1. Scan lines top-to-bottom

3. When `#endregion` is found, pop from stack and save a `{start, end, name}` entry

1552026-03-11T19:00:20.795235agentmessage-
All four tasks complete. Here is a precise account of everything that was written and why each decision was made.

---

## What was implemented

### 1. `namedFoldingRegionProvider.ts` (new file)

**Regex patterns**
```ts
const REGION_PATTERN   = /^\s*#region\b\s*(.*)/i;
const ENDREGION_PATTERN = /^\s*#endregion\b/i;
```
- `\s*` at the start handles indented markers (common in Python, shell, CSS).
- `\b` prevents matching `#regions` (spurious plurals).
- The `/i` flag gives case-insensitive matching (`#REGION`, `#Region`, etc.).
- Group `(.*)` captures everything after `#region`, which is then `.trim()`-ed to strip trailing whitespace.

**`getNamedRegions(model)`**  
Stack-based scan (identical strategy to `IndentRangeProvider`). Each `#region` is pushed with its line number and name; each matching `#endregion` pops the stack and emits a `NamedRegion`. Unmatched openers (no `#endregion` before EOF) are silently discarded because they remain on the stack and are never emitted. The result is sorted ascending by `startLine`, satisfying `FoldingRegions`' constructor requirement.

**`computeNamedRegions(model, foldingRangesLimit)`**  
Converts the `NamedRegion[]` array into the `Uint32Array` pair required by `new FoldingRegions(...)`, respecting the `foldingRangesLimit.limit` ceiling and calling `foldingRangesLimit.update()` so the existing limit-reporting UI works automatically. Region names go into the `types` array so they surface via `result.getType(i)` in the folding model.

**`NAMED_REGION_START_DECORATION` + `applyNamedRegionDecorations()`**  
Uses `ModelDecorationOptions.register` with `linesDecorationsClassName: 'named-region-start'` (the CSS class added in `folding.css`) and `TrackedRangeStickiness.NeverGrowsWhenTypingAtEdges` so the decoration stays on exactly the 
... (truncated)

Now let me think about the circular dependency concern:
- `folding.ts` imports `namedFoldingRegionProvider.ts` (side-effect only)
- `namedFoldingRegionProvider.ts` imports `RangeProvider` and `FoldingLimitReporter` from `folding.ts`

This creates a circular dependency: `folding.ts` → `namedFoldingRegionProvider.ts` → `folding.ts`.

In Node.js/bundlers, circular imports are generally handled, but they can cause issues if a symbol is used before it's initialized. Let me think about this more carefully:

When `folding.ts` is first loaded:
1. It starts executing imports from top to bottom
2. When it hits `import './namedFoldingRegionProvider.js'`, Node starts loading that module
3. `namedFoldingRegionProvider.ts` tries to import `RangeProvider` and `FoldingLimitReporter` from `./folding.js`
4. At this point, `folding.ts` is partially loaded (it's in the process of being loaded), so the circular import returns what has been exported so far
5. `RangeProvider` and `FoldingLimitReporter` are interfaces (TypeScript types), which are erased at runtime — so they don't exist at runtime at all. They're just type imports. At runtime, there's nothing to import from `folding.js` for those types — they'll be erased.

All four tasks are complete and committed. Here is a precise summary of every change made and the rationale behind each design decision.

---

## What was implemented

### 1. `namedFoldingRegionProvider.ts` (199 lines) — *new file*

**Exported API**

| Symbol | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `NamedRegion` | Plain data interface `{ name, startLine, endLine }` |
| `getNamedRegions(model)` | Scans every line for `#region`/`#endregion`, returns sorted `NamedRegion[]`; unmatched markers are silently discarded |
| `computeNamedRegions(model, reporter)` | Wraps `getNamedRegions`, packs results into a `FoldingRegions(Uint32Array, Uint32Array, string[])` and calls `reporter.update()` to honour the folding-ranges limit |
| `applyNamedRegionDecorations(editor, regions, existing)` | Stamps a `named-region-start` gutter decoration on each `#region` start line; returns the new decoration IDs for later cleanup |
| `NamedFoldingRegionProvider` | Implements `RangeProvider` (`id = 'namedRegion'`); delegates to `computeNamedRegions` |
| `GoToNamedRegionAction` | `EditorAction` with command id `editor.action.goToNamedRegion`; shows a quick-pick list, preview-scrolls on hover (`onDidFocus`), and navigates on confirmation; cleans up decorations unconditionally |

**Key decisions**
- **Regex patterns** — `REGION_PATTERN = /^\s*#region\b\s*(.*)/i` and `ENDREGION_PATTERN = /^\s*#endregion\b/i` handle leading whitespace, case-insensitivity, and guard against partial-word false positives (`\b`).
- **Stack-based nesting** — a LIFO stack pairs each `#endregion` with the most recent unclosed `#region`, giving correct nested-region semantics.
- **Default name** — when `#region` has no trailing text the region is named `region <lineNumber>` (matches VS Code's own convention).
- **Limit reporting** — mirrors th
... (truncated)

### Architecture walkthrough

**`getNamedRegions(model)`** — pure scanning function  
Uses a LIFO stack: each `#region` line pushes `{ line, name }`, each `#endregion` pops and emits a `NamedRegion`. Unmatched openers are discarded when the stack is non-empty at EOF. The two regex patterns use `\b` to avoid partial-word false positives and `i` flag for case-insensitivity, and `^\s*` to tolerate any indentation level.

**`computeNamedRegions(model, reporter)`** — folding engine integration  
Packs `NamedRegion[]` into the `FoldingRegions(Uint32Array, Uint32Array, string[])` constructor. The `types[]` array carries region names so `FoldingRegions.getType(i)` and `hasTypes()` both work correctly. Calls `reporter.update(computed, limited | false)` exactly once, matching the contract of every other built-in range provider.

**`NamedFoldingRegionProvider`** — `RangeProvider` implementation  
`id = 'namedRegion'`, `compute()` checks `isCancellationRequested` before delegating. Ready to be instantiated by any code that wants to register it with the `FoldingController`.

**`applyNamedRegionDecorations`** — gutter marker  
Uses a static `ModelDecorationOptions` instance (`NeverGrowsWhenTypingAtEdges`) with `linesDecorationsCla
